} &lt;/style&gt; &lt;p&gt; A system has 25 magnetic tape drives and 5 processes : P1, P2, P3, P4, P5. The allocation of resources and the need for the resources by the processes are described in the table. Which of the following is possible &lt;b&gt;safe state&lt;/b&gt; of the system?&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&lt;i&gt;Hint&lt;/i&gt;: A system is in a &lt;b&gt;safe state&lt;/b&gt; if there is a sequence in which all the processes can be executed without getting into a &lt;b&gt;deadlock&lt;/b&gt;. &lt;/p&gt; Adding up the heights of the bottles on a stack will give you the overall height of the stack. &lt;pre&gt; A CPU scheduler executes processes in time quantum of 100ms and then calculates the next process to execute after each quantum. 3 processes are fed into our CPU&#39;s process scheduler with the following attributes Process A Arrival Time: 0 Execution Time Needed: 1300msec Process B Arrival Time: 500msec Execution Time Needed: 1100msec Process C Arrival Time: 700msec Execution Time Needed: 1500msec There are four main algorithms which our CPU uses to schedule processes: FCFR: First Come First Serve SJF: Shortest Job First SRTF: Shortest Remaining Time First RR: Round Robin If the scheduler is using the RR algorithm to schedule processes, which processes would have been completed after 3600 ms? &lt;/pre&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:ArbisoftX+AFGT02+2020_T1+type@problem+block@cf807c7412e36261f5c6-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt; &lt;p&gt; A &lt;b&gt;min-heap&lt;/b&gt; is a heap where the value of each internal node is smaller than or equal to the values of its children. Consider a binary &lt;b&gt;min-heap&lt;/b&gt; implemented using an array as follows: The root is stored in the first location, &lt;b&gt;a[0]&lt;/b&gt;, nodes in the next level, from left to right, is stored from &lt;b&gt;a[1]&lt;/b&gt; to &lt;b&gt;a[2]&lt;/b&gt;. The nodes from the second level of the tree from left to right are stored from &lt;b&gt;a[3]&lt;/b&gt; location onward... &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:ArbisoftX+AFGT02+2020_T1+type@problem+block@6f33c045090169dffc8d-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt; &lt;p&gt;There are two storage systems present, one is a stack and the other queue. The content of the stack is &lt;strong&gt;[3, 0, 11, 4]&lt;/strong&gt; and the content of the queue is &lt;strong&gt;[22, 16, 20, 26, 23, 24, 29, 21, 15, 27]&lt;/strong&gt; (the first item in both represent the first item stored). The number on each item represent the ID of item. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;We have to balance these storage systems (move items between storages so that there are equal number of items in both). Keeping in mind the functionalities of stacks and queues, we have to balance them! &lt;/p&gt; &lt;pre&gt; &lt;h3&gt;STACK STORAGE: &lt;i&gt;oldest&lt;/i&gt; &lt;strong&gt; [3, 0, 11, 4] &lt;/strong&gt; &lt;i&gt;newest&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/h3&gt; &lt;h3&gt;QUEUE STORAGE: &lt;i&gt;oldest&lt;/i&gt; &lt;strong&gt; [22, 16, 20, 26, 23, 24, 29, 21, 15, 27] &lt;/strong&gt; &lt;i&gt;newest&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/h3&gt; &lt;/pre&gt; &lt;div id=&#34;tree&#34; style=&#34;height: 700px; width: 100%&#34;&gt; &lt;/div&gt; &lt;script src=&#34;/assets/courseware/v1/9fcabde300dca784e0cf1ab86719f851/asset-v1:ArbisoftX+AFGT02+2020_T1+type@asset+block/d3.v3.js&#34; type=&#34;text/javascript&#34;/&gt; &lt;script type=&#34;text/javascript&#34;&gt; var treeData = [{&#34;name&#34;: &#34;E&#34;, &#34;children&#34;: [{&#34;name&#34;: &#34;P&#34;, &#34;children&#34;: [{&#34;name&#34;: &#34;T&#34;}, {&#34;name&#34;: &#34;O&#34;, &#34;children&#34;: [{&#34;name&#34;: &#34;Y&#34;, &#34;children&#34;: [{&#34;name&#34;: &#34;Q&#34;}, &#34;&#34;]}, &#34;&#34;]}]}, {&#34;name&#34;: &#34;X&#34;, &#34;children&#34;: [&#34;&#34;, {&#34;name&#34;: &#34;W&#34;}]}]}]; // ************** Generate the tree diagram ***************** var margin = {top: 40, right: 120, bottom: 20, left: 120}, width = 960 - margin.right - margin.left, height = 500 - margin.top - margin.bottom; var i = 0; var tree = d3.layout.tree() .size([height, width]); var diagonal = d3.svg.diagonal() .projection(function(d) { return [d.x, d.y]; }); var svg = d3.select(&#34;#tree&#34;).append(&#34;svg&#34;) .attr(&#34;width&#34;, &#34;100%&#34;) .attr(&#34;height&#34;, &#34;700px&#34;) .append(&#34;g&#34;) .attr(&#34;transform&#34;, &#34;translate(&#34; + margin.left + &#34;,&#34; + margin.top + &#34;)&#34;); root = treeData[0]; update(root); function update(source) { // Compute the new tree layout. var nodes = tree.nodes(root).reverse(), links = tree.links(nodes); // Normalize for fixed-depth. nodes.forEach(function(d) { d.y = d.depth * 100; }); // Declare the nodes&amp;#8230; var node = svg.selectAll(&#34;g.node&#34;) .data(nodes, function(d) { return d.id || (d.id = ++i); }); // Enter the nodes. var nodeEnter = node.enter().append(&#34;g&#34;) .attr(&#34;class&#34;, &#34;node&#34;) .attr(&#34;transform&#34;, function(d) { return &#34;translate(&#34; + d.x + &#34;,&#34; + d.y + &#34;)&#34;; }); nodeEnter.append(&#34;text&#34;) .attr(&#34;dy&#34;, &#34;.35em&#34;) .attr(&#34;text-anchor&#34;, &#34;middle&#34;) .text(function(d) { return d.name; }) .style(&#34;fill-opacity&#34;, 1) .style(&#34;font-size&#34;, &#34;2em&#34;); // Declare the links&amp;#8230; var link = svg.selectAll(&#34;path.link&#34;) .data(links, function(d) { return d.target.id; }); // Enter the links. link.enter().insert(&#34;path&#34;, &#34;g&#34;) .attr(&#34;class&#34;, &#34;link&#34;) .attr(&#34;d&#34;, diagonal); &lt;p&gt; Anaya has three Urdu novels &lt;strong&gt;(F, C, D)&lt;/strong&gt; and Four English novels &lt;strong&gt;(A, B, E, G)&lt;/strong&gt;. She wants to arrange her novels in a way that following conditions must be met: &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;- No english novel can be placed immediate after another english novel.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;- D must be placed earlier than E.&lt;/p&gt; Inheritance

1 point possible (graded, results hidden)

What should be the result of running the following pseudocode snippet? 

      
class Class1:
    function function_1(self):
         print("a")

    function function_2(self):
         print("b")


class Class2:
    function function_1(self):
         print("c")

    function function_3(self):
         print("d")


class Class3:
    function function_2(self):
         print("e")

    function function_3(self):
         print("f")


class ClassA(Class3, Class1):
    function function_3(self):
         print("h")


class ClassB(Class2):
    function function_2(self):
         print("i")

    function function_3(self):
         print("j")


class ClassC(Class1):
    function function_2(self):
         print("k")

    function function_3(self):
         print("l")
      
      
ClassA().function_2()
ClassC().function_2()
ClassA().function_3()

Process Scheduling

1 point possible (graded, results hidden)
    
A CPU scheduler executes processes in time quantum of 100ms and then calculates the next process to execute after each quantum.
3 processes are fed into our CPU's process scheduler with the following attributes

Process A
Arrival Time: 0
Execution Time Needed: 1300msec

Process B
Arrival Time: 500msec
Execution Time Needed: 1100msec

Process C
Arrival Time: 700msec
Execution Time Needed: 1500msec

There are four main algorithms which our CPU uses to schedule processes:
FCFR: First Come First Serve
SJF:  Shortest Job First
SRTF: Shortest Remaining Time First
RR:   Round Robin

If the scheduler is using the RR algorithm to schedule processes, which processes would have been completed after 3600 ms?

Employee salaries

1 point possible (graded, results hidden)
Table: employee_age
emp_id age
100 30
103 32
101 31
102 24
Table: employee_salary
emp_id salary
104 35000
103 45000
100 70000
102 49000

With given tables what would be output of following SQL query: 


SELECT 
    MIN(eSal.salary)
FROM 
    employee_age as eAge INNER JOIN employee_salary as eSal
ON 
    eAge.emp_id = eSal.emp_id

    WHERE eAge.age > 24
GROUP BY eAge.emp_id
    HAVING MIN(eSal.salary) > 35000

class A:
    def __init__(self):
        self.calc_i(246)

        self.i = 14 * i;

class B(A):
    def __init__(self):
        super().__init__()
        print("i from B is", self.i)
        
    def calc_i(self, i):
        self.i = 62 * i;

b = B()

Round and round

1 point possible (graded, results hidden)

We have come upon a 'longRunning' method in our code. In order to check its lengthy execution time, we are calculating its iterations it against different inputs.

Can you figure out the number of iterations it will take to execute the following input:

[9, 4, 19, 0] 

       function longRunningFunction(array) {
   for ( i = 0; i < length(array); i++ ) {
 	idx = i
 	for ( j = i + 1; j < length(array); j++ ) {
   	if ( array[idx] > array[j] ) {
     	idx = j
   	}
 	}
 	swap( array[i], array[idx] )
   }
 }
